BLOOD ADMINISTERED: None.

ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS: Minimal. She had about 200 mL of intra-abdominal blood. COMPLICATIONS: Nona.

ANESTHESTA; General,

SURGEON: Travis Gilbert, DO.

GRAFTS OR IMPLANTS: None.

DESCRIPTION OF PROCEDURE: The patisant was taken to the operating room, given general anesthesia, prepped and draped in the dorsal lithotomy position using Allen stirrups. The patient was sterilely prepared and draped. The bladder was drained. A manipulator was placed into the uterus. The surgeon was regloved and attention was made to the abdomen. I made a 5 mm incision into the umbilicus and inserted an Optiview trocar into the ahdomen under direct visualization using laparoscope. We filled the abdomen with cO2 gas up to i5 mmHg and placed an 8 mm trocar suprapubically in the midline and a 5 mm trocar to the left.

OPERATIVE FINDINGS:

1. Hemoperitonsum.

2. The left fallopian tube was swollen with an ectopic and was bleeding out “he end, The ends appeared to hava blunting.

wH&SCRIPTION OF PROCEDURE: We first used to the Enseal device to grasp under the fallopian tube, across the broad ligament sealing and cutting as we went along. We excised the entire fallopian tube. We placed it into a bag and removed it through the 8 mm port. We then suctioned all tha blood out of the abdomen. Irrigated, placed some Marcaine in tha pelvis for postoperative pain control,

CLINICAL DATA: PROVISIONAL DX: LEFT PELVIC PAIN.

DIAGNOSIS: LEFT FALLOPIAN TUBE: ECTOPIC (TUBAL) PREGNANCY WITH ASSOCIATED HEMORRHAGE AND CHRONIC INFLAMMATION.

SPECIMEN SITE: LEFT FALLOPIAN TUBE

GROSS DESCRIPTION:

Specimen consists of a portion of distended, gray brown hemorrhagic fallopian tube measuring approximately 5 cm in length and ranging in diameter from 3 mm to 1.2 om. A disrupted area is present, from which gray tan papillary type tissue protrudes, measuring up to 1 cmin diameter. Serial sectioning reveals distention of the tubal lumen by hemorrhagic clot material. A detached fragment of clot material is also received in the specimen container, measuring up to 2 x 1.3.x 0.8 cm. Tan papillary tissue is focally seen at the edge of the clot material. There is also a third piece of tissue which is tan and glistening and measures 1.5 x 0.8 x 0.5 cm. Sectioning reveals a pinpoint lumen, suggestive of proximal tube. Multiple representative sections are submitted in two blocks. (CM)

MICROSCOPIC DESCRIPTION: Microscopic examination performed.

ECTOPIC PREGNANCY With SALPINGECTOMY.

An ectopic pregnancy is a pregnancy that occurs outside of the uterus, The fertilized egg started growing in your fallopian tube instead of your uterus. Many times It is unknown why this occurs but most often happens when the tubes narrow. The fertilized egg cannot survive and must be surgically removed, Complete healing will take several weeks.

{includes ‘Female reproductive system showing possible ectopic pregnancy sites’ graphic)

There is an incision Into your abdomen to remove the section or all of the atfected fallopian tube. This witl end your present pregnancy. Yaur ability ta get pregnant again is slightly decreased with one tube instead of two tubes. You CAN get pregnant again with one fallopian tube.

Follow these instructions; Slowly increase your activity, Take short walks and get plenty of rest, Climb stairs slowly and use the hand rail. No pushing, pulling or straining (vacuuming, shoveling, sweeping etc.) You may take a shower in AM after your procedure.. Check with your doctor befare driving. Check with your docter before resuming sexual activity. Do not use douches, tampons or hava intercourse for 6 weeks unless otherwise instructad. * To avoid trouble with constipation: * Orink at teast 8 glasses of water or juice each day unless your Doctor has limited your fluids. * Eat high fiber foods (whole graln breads and cereals, vegetables and fruits). * Call a support program called for suppor in helping you manage through this loss of your pregnancy. * Work with your doctor as you ptan future pregnancies.

Call your doctor if you have:

trouble passing your urine.

Increased bleeding or drainage trom your incisien, swelling, redness or opening of your incision. foul small from your incision or dressing. increased or foul smefiing vagina! discharge. chills or fever over 101 degrees (by mouth). pain not helped by your pain medicine.

pain in your calf er leg.

trouble or pain with breathing.

Increased nausea or vomiting.

IRON SUPPLEMENTS (Ferraus Sulfate - Feosol or Fer-In-Sol, Ferrous Fumarate - Feostat, Ferrous Gtuconate - Fergon, Iron Dextran - DexFerrum , lron Polysaccharide - Niferex, Iron Sucrose - Venofer, others)

Take this medicine by mouth in the following dose: 1 tablet 2 times a day,

This is an iron supplement. Iron |s a mineral that you normally get through the food you eat. Itis used to treat some kinds of anemia (not enough iron in the bload). iron is needed to form healthy red blood cells. This medicine may be used for cther reasons, as prescribed by your doctor.

Side effecta may include:

* diarrhea

* heartburn

* upsel stomach

* constipation

« loss of appetite

Other sida effects may occur, but are not as common. Signs of allergy may Include: facial or throat swelling, rash, wheezing or shortness of breath.

Follow these Instructions:

* Do not take antacids or caicium supplements at the same time as this medicine. Take antacids and calcium supplements 1 hour before or 2 hours after the iran supplement.

* Do not crush sustained release (SR} capsules.

* This medicine works best if you take it on an empty stomach (1 hour before or2 hours aftar meats). If this causes an upset stomach, you may take it with food.

« Expect your bowe! movements to be black in color while taking this iran supplament. This is not harmful.

« Certain foods dacrease this medicine's affect on your body. Do not eat the fotlowing within two hours of the iron supplement:

* eggs * cheese * milk

° coffee * tea

* If you will ba having lab tests while taking this medicine, lel! the person in charge that you are taking an Iron supplement. Iron can affect lab resulta, especially when looking for blood in the bowel movements.

¢ tfyou are taking the liquid solution, mix each dose in water or fruil juice and drink it from a straw. This helps keep the iron off your teeth, sinca liquid iron can stain your teeth.

* Keep all follow-up appointments with your doctor.

* Store this medicine atroom temperature, away from heat, moisture or direct light.

* Store this medicine away from children's reach. This medicine can ba dangerous if a child takes too much of it,

* Ifyou are taking this medicine on a regular schedule and miss adose, take it as soon as you remember it. If it is almnst time for your next dose, skip the missed dose. Do not double the doses.

+ You save money and your taste and smell will improve.

How to quit?

« Be sure lo have a strong support group such as: family, friends, co-worker, and your doctor,

+ Eat healthy, stay active and change your routine to distract yourself from smoking.

* Smoking/Tobacco use is expensive, increases the aging process, and second hand smoke hurts your family and friends.

What are the Benefits of Quitting?

* Your chances of getting cancer decrease.

* Your chance of heart attack decreases within 24 hours.

« You save money and your taste and smell will improve.

How to quit?

» Set a quit date and stick to it-not a single puff more.

» Be sure to have a strong support group such as: family, friends, co-worker, and your doctor.

Global Patient Safety

The staff of Baptist Health Corbin regards your safety as a priority. We take several precautions to assure your safety during you stay. We require all hospital staff to wear photo identification badges, so all our patients know who we are. Therefore, we ask that you follow these guidelines:

Should you leave the floor for personal reasons, please follow these guidelines:

Notify staff when leaving the floor.

Go to the nurses’ station to sign out.

When you return to the floor please sign back in on the log book at the nurses station.

If you have not returned to your room by the time you have given us, we will initiate our “Code Purple” to locate you, to assure your safety. “Code Purple” alerts our staff to search for missing patients.

PON

We thank you for choosing Baptist Health Corbin for your health care needs.

BLOOD TRANSFUSION AND BLOOD PRODUCTS RISKS, BENEFITS, & ALTERNATIVES-If you wish not to receive blood or blood products please request to sign a refusal form. 1) Some surgical procedures may require blood transfusions or blocd products. My doctor has informed me that I may need to have blood products administered during the course of my treatment. 2) It has been explained to me that the administration of blood products involves the introduction of the product into one of my veins, commonly in the arm using a needle. I understand that the amount of blood preducts administered is determined by my doctor based upon my particular needs. 3) It has been explained to me that the administration of blood products may expose me to certain risks. Minor or temporary reactions, such as slight bruising, swelling, or Jocal infection of the area where the needle pierces the skin is not urrcommon. Non-serious reactions may include headache, fever, or a mild skin reaction, such as itching or a rash. Rare, but serious reactions are possible such as the transmission of diseases including hepatitis and AIDS, which require lengthy treatment and can be fatal. It has been further explained that while procedures for screening blood products for diseases such as AIDS and hepatitis are effective, these procedures are not perfect and there is a risk of exposure to AIDS, hepatitis, or other blood-bome disease. I have taken all of these risks into consideration and have decided that the benefits of receiving blood products outweigh the risks. 4) I have been made aware of the reasonably available alternatives to the administration of blood products and the risks and benefits of those alternatives including autologous blood transfusion, directed donation and not having any blood products administered. I understand that I may be able to donate one of several units of my own blood to be used during planned elective surgery and that my doctor must determine my ability to donate for myself. This is called autologous transfusion.

If I choose to have an autologous transfusion, I understand that the last unit of blood must be donated one week prior to expected use. Talso understand that I may choose a directed donation. A directed donation means I] am allowed to select

ANESTHESIA-I understand that this procedure may require anesthesia. An anesthesiologist has or will explain the anesthesia alternatives, Complications from any type of anesthetic are infrequent, but do occur. Complications are more frequent for patients in poor health than for patients in good health. Complications associated with all types of anesthesia include temporary or permanent damage to teeth, lips, nose, throat, voice box, windpipe, eyes, nerves, or blood vessels. Drug reaction may occur and may be minor or serious even requiring resuscitation, Breathing problems may develop.

Headache, back pain, some degree of awareness, infection, nausea and/or vomiting may occur. There are some very serious complications, which are uncommon, but can occur. These include paralysis, brain damage, or death. There are other potential complications depending on your situation; however, it is not possible to advise you of every imaginable complication. The purpose of this is not to frighten you, but to properly inform you. Serious complications are unlikely. The benefits of surgery and anesthesia, except in extreme circumstances, outweigh the potential risks. 1 agree that the potential benefit of the procedure(s) outweighs the potential risks of anesthesia.

Tt understand that my procedure is scheduled to be done with one of the following:

General Anesthesia-monitoring and care provided by the anesthesiologist with or without a CRNA

Monitored Anesthesia Care-possible sedation, monitoring and care provided by the anesthesiologist or a CRNA Regional Anesthesia-monitoring and care provided by the anesthesiologist or a CRNA Local Anesthesia-care managed by the Physician and monitored by 4 registered nurse Moderate Sedation-care managed by the Physician and monitored by a registered nurse

Deoadoa

I understand that I must be: 1.) Accompanied by a responsible adult.

2.) Not take public transportation without the presence of another adule.

3.) Not drive a car, ingest alcoholic beverages, or depressant medication without direct permission from the physician, for a minimum of 24 hours.

4.) Not make any important decisions or sign any important documents or checks for 24 to 36 hours

There is the possibility that any of the services provided above may convert to a general anesthetic. These same complications may occur with local anesthesia. It may become necessary for the anesthesiologist to render care ina life-threatening emergency situation without my previous consent. If during a local anesthetic an emergent situation arises I understand that my physician may consult with an anesthesiologist to render the necessary emergency medical care.

2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL:

In most situations, the medical treatment provided to patients in the Hospital is given by physicians and other providers who are not employees or agents of the Hospital. Such providers include, but are not limited to, anesthesiologists, cardiologists, radiologists, emergency physicians, pathologists surgeons, certified registered nurse anesthetists, nurse praciitioners, physician assistants, surgical assistants and psychologists. These providers may be independent or may be employed by other health care organizations. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers or the Hospital bill you receive may have separate charges for services of such Providers. Charges for such services are established by these providers.

3. CONSENT TO USE AND DISCLOSURE OF INFORMATION:

| authorize the Hospital and the health care providers on its medical staff to use and disclose information about me to carry out treatment, payment and healthcare operations. TOBACCO FREE ENVIRONMENT

Baptist Health supports wellness and health by maintaining a “Tobacco Free” campus environment. Our “Tobacco Free” environment has been established to minimize adverse health effects to everyone with whom we have contact. This policy applies to all tobacco products including cigarettes, cigars, pipes, herbal tobacco products and chewing tobacco. These items are prohibited from use on Baptist Health's campus or at any facility owned, leased or operated by Baptist (Excluding Paducah, as there are designated smoking areas). | understand that | will need to communicate with my treating physician or nurse to request nicotine replacement products, if needed. | understand that 1 am to remain in my treatment area at all times. | further understand that if i leave my treatment area or any Baptist Health Facility, that | wilt not be under nursing or medical supervision and may aggravate or worsen my condition and may complicate or interfere with the course of treatment prescribed by my physician.

SMOKING CESSATION

Wellness and Health Promotion: for smokers, those who are around smokers (second-hand smoke), or those who quit smoking and failed.

Smoking cessation ts quitting smoking. Smoking is a very difficult habit to break for most people. The chemical, nicotine, which you inhale into your lungs from a cigarette, causes your brain to have more dopamine. Dopamine Is a chemical that makes you fee! good. Nicotine has many more harmful effects on your body. This is why it is so important to stop smoking. Nicotine is addictive, which means when your body is used to having nicotine, and then nicotine isn't there, you feel strong physical cravings and a need to smoke. This is why stopping is so difficult.

Why is smoking bad for me?

e Smoking increases your chance for having a heart attack, a stroke and/or cancer.

* Smoking decreases the amount of oxygen that gets to your brain, heart, and other organs.

* Smoking raises your blood pressure and makes it harder for your blood to circulate throughout your body. . Smoking increases acid in your stomach, which leads to ulcers

" Why is quitting good for me?

As soon as you quit smoking, your chances of having a heart attack, stroke, and other diseases start to go down. The langer you do not smoke, the smailer your risk for these diseases and problems.

What is the best way to quit? First, decide in your mind that you are going to quit.

Set a specific date to stop smoking and tell other people that you are going to stop smoking on your quit date.

Talk to your doctor about medications that can be used to help you quit. Over the counter and prescription are available. Talk to ex-smokers about what helped them quit.

Join a support group for peeple who are quitting. Group participation raises your chance of success by eight times. Find friends or family members who are willing to help you quit or who wili quit smoking with you.

Before your quit date, only allow yourself to smoke in one or two places.

Pay attention to when, where, and with whom you smoke. Notice what things make you feel like smoking.

Avoid the places, situations, and people that cause you to want a cigarette, at least at first when you are quitting. Make a list of all of the good things that will happen if you quit smoking.

Think of what you will do with the money that you will save by not buying cigarettes.

Begin an exercise program suggested by your doctor.

Throw away all cigarettes, lighters, and matches before your quit date.

Date: 7-)F—-17

For Additional Help, please contact the Kentucky Quit Line: 1-860-Quit Now (1-[PHONE-1269]) or TDY/TDD 1-[PHONE-1270]

Reason: This is a 28-year-old female with right rib pain. Patient had trauma to the right ribs.

PROCEDURE: Single view of the chest and 3 dedicated right rib detail images are presented

FINDINGS : The chest radiograph shows no evidence of pneumothorax. The lungs are clear. There is evidence of scoliosis.

snree rib detail images show no plain radiographic evidence of acute rib fracture. There are no blastic or lytic lesions.

IMPRESSION: Scoliosis. No post traumatic changes identified on today's plain radiographs

MEDICATION: VICODIN (Hydrocodone) VICODIN (generic: Hydrocodone + acetaminophen) is a narcotic pain medicine, —“it dis also available under the trade names LORTAB and ANEXSIA, NORCO.

TRECTIONS FOR USE:

£ this medicine makes your stomach upset, take it with food. Pain medication should be taken only if needed at the times prescribed. If you are not having pain, do not take the medicine, unless you are advised to do so by your doctor. WHAT TO WATCH FOR:

POSSIBLE SIDE EEFECTS: Dizziness, drowsiness -- > (Take a smaller dose; for example, break the pill in half or taka it less often). Constipation -- > (Drink lots of liquids, use small doses of a mild laxative like Milk of Magnesia, as neaded). Nausea, vomiting -- > (Take with food). Difficulty passing urine-- > (Stop the medicine and contact your doctor). ALLERGIC REACTION: Rash, itching, swelling, trouble breathing or swallowing -- > (Contact your doctor or return to this facility promptly).

RKKKKAIKKK TMPORTANT ek tok RK KK MEDICAL CONDITIONS: Before starting this medicine, be sure your doctor knows if you have any of the following conditions:

-- Prostate enlargement

-- Pregnancy or breast feeding

DRUG INTERACTIONS: This drug may cause increased side effects when taken with alcohol, muscle relaxant, sedative, tricyclic antidepressant, MAO-inhibitor or another pain medicine. WARNINGS :

~~ DO NOT DRIVE, ride a bicycle or operate dangerous equipment while taking this medicine until you know how it will affect you.

-- Prolonged use of this medicine can be HABIT FORMING and may lead to ADDICTION.

(NOTE: This information topic may not include all directions, precautions, medical conditions, drug/food interactions and warnings for this drug. Check with your doctor, nurse or pharmacist for any questions that you may have. ]

Smoking/Tobacco use can cause Cancer, Heart and Lung Disease. + Smoking/Tobacce use is expensive, increases the aging process, and second hand smoke hurts your family and friends. Smoking/Tobacco Cessation Counseling.

This is for educational purposes only, If you have any questions, please discuss them with your nurse. The receipt of this form will NOT affect your insurance benefits or hospital bill.

Why Should You Stop Smoking or Using Tobacco? Smoking/Tobacco use causes CANCER to grow. Smoking/Tobacco use causes HEART and LUNG DISEASE. Smoking/Tobacco use is EXPENSIVE.

Smoking/Tobacco use quickens the AGING process. Second-hand smoke HURTS your family and friends. Smoking damages TASTEBUDS and discolors your TEETH and NAILS. Smoking increases NERVOUSNESS.

What are the Benefits of Quitting?

Your chances of getting cancer decrease.

Your chance of heart attack decreases within 24 hours. YOU SAVE MONEY!

Your taste and smell will improve.

You will have more energy.

= You will live longer! How to Quit: Ready — Set a quit date and stick to it —not a single puff more.

Set ~ Get support from family, friends, co-workers, doctor, or other health care providers — get group, individual, or telephone counseling.

Go — Learn new ways to live healthy:

= Change your routine to distract yourself from smoking.

« Reduce stress.

= Eat a healthy diet and stay active.

= Drink plenty of water and other fluids. Medication That Can Help: Falk to your healthcare provider about whether medication is right for you. Common medications available to help you quit:

« ZYBAN — www. zyban. com — available by prescription

« Nicotine gum — www. nicorettegum, com — available over-the-counter

= Nicotine inhaler — available by prescription

* Nicotine nasal spray — www. nicobrevin. com — available by prescription

« Nicotine patch —www.nicodermCQ. com — available over-the-counter

For More Information:

« American Heart Association [PHONE-1333]

* American Lung Association [PHONE-1334] or 1-800-LUNG-USA = Cooper — Clayion Smoking Cessation Program [PHONE-1335] Sponsored by BRMC/Laurel County Health Department

if you are a non-smoker, please feel free to share this information with a family member or friend.

No guarantee has bean given to me as to the results that may be obtained from my care.

2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE INDEPENDENT PRACTITIONERS:

In mest situations, the medical treatment provided to patients in the Hospital is provided by physicians who are independent practitioners and not employees or agents of the Hospital. Independent practitioners may include, but are not limited to, anesthesiclogists, cardiologists, radiologists, emergency room physicians, pathologists, surgeons and surgical assistants. There are also other health care providers in the Hospital who are not employees or agents of the Hospital Including, but not limited to certified registered nurse anesthetists, nurse practitioners, Physician assistants, and psychologists. You will receive a separate bill for these services or the Hospital bill you receive will have separate charges for services of physicians and other Independent practitioners, Charges for these services are established by the physicians and other independent practitioners.

3. CONSENT TO USE AND DISCLOSURE OF INFORMATION:

| authorize the Hospital and the independent practitioners on its medical staff to use and disclose Information about me to carry out treatment, payment and healthcare operations. Examples of such uses and disclosures include, but are not limited to, providing information to: (a) any person, company, or entity (such as HMOs, insurance companies, workers’ compensation carriers, my employer, the Medicare and Medicaid programs and their intermediaries and review organizations, and any other payor or its review organization or third party administrator) that is or may be flable for paying any claim fer benefits arising out of services provided to me on an inpatient or outpatient basis, or for any ambulance services provided for my transport to or from the Hospital; (b) any independent practitioner or ambulance company providing services for me; (c) any providers who may be providing follow-up care to me after discharge such as home haalth agencies, nursing homes, and physiclans: (d) any licensing or accrediting organizations necessary for the Hospital to obtain or maintain licensure or accreditation; and (e) any other persons or entities described in the Hospital’s Notice of Privacy Practices, This consent includes the telease of medical records and billing information related to drug-related congitions, alccholism, psychological and psychiatric conditions, and/or communicable or blood-borne Infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV). | also consent to any third party payor or its review organization paying for my care to discuss my plan of treatment for utilization review purposes. | alsa authorize the release of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act.
